# data load / preview
import pandas as pd
import numpy as np

train_df = pd.read_csv('movie_ratings.csv')
train_df.drop(columns=['Unnamed: 0'], inplace=True)
test_df = pd.read_csv('movie_ratings_question.csv')
rating_ids = test_df['ratingId']
test_df = test_df[['userId', 'movieId']] # keep only user and movie id

# movie metadata
movies_df = pd.read_csv('movies.csv')
# tags - user generated descriptions
tags_df = pd.read_csv('tags.csv')
# links - imdb and tmdb data for movies
# note: imdb and tmbd do not affect the models since they are just id references to external ratings
# 
links_df = pd.read_csv('links.csv')

print(train_df.shape)
print(test_df.shape)

movies_encoded = movies_exploded[['movieId']].join(genres_encoded)

# integrate tags.csv features
# TfidfVectorizer converts text to number vectors based on how common the tag appears in the data
# can use cosine similarity on similar keywords
from sklearn.feature_extraction.text import TfidfVectorizer

grouped_tags = tags_df.groupby("movieId", as_index=False)["tag"].agg(" ".join)

tf_vectorizer = TfidfVectorizer(stop_words="english")
tag_matrix = tf_vectorizer.fit_transform(grouped_tags["tag"])
tags = pd.DataFrame(tag_matrix.toarray(), index=grouped_tags["movieId"])
In[102]:
# merge genre (movies_features) with the tags
movies_features = movies_features.set_index('movieId')
mf_tags = movies_features.join(tags, how='left').fillna(0)
merged_features = mf_tags.reset_index()
# merge imdb and tmdb into merged_features
merged_features = pd.merge(merged_features, links_df, on='movieId', how='left')
merged_features.drop(columns=['imdbId', 'tmdbId'], inplace=True, errors='ignore')

from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import cosine_similarity

# create a matrix for genre cos similarity
genre_matrix = merged_features.set_index('movieId')
genre_similarity_matrix = pd.DataFrame(cosine_similarity(genre_matrix), index=genre_matrix.index, columns=genre_matrix.index)
#print(genre_similarity_matrix.head())

# Combine genre with tags_df features
In[107]:
# function for predictingd on cos similarity (content based)
# from week 11: recommender pdf: says to use movie profiles and comparing them to user preferences.
# so use cosine_similarity on genres (above)
# build movie profiles based on genre and user profiles based on their previous behaviour
# weigh the averages of similar ratings
def predict_rating_content_based(user_id, movie_id, k=20):
    if movie_id not in genre_similarity_matrix.columns:
        print("movie not found in dataset")
        return np.nan
    
    # get the movies that the user has ALREADY rated
    user_rated_movies = train_merged[train_merged['userId'] == user_id]
    if user_rated_movies.empty:
        print("user hasnt rated any movies yet")
        return np.nan
    
    # rank the similarity of this movie to their previouslyt rated movies
    similarity = genre_similarity_matrix.loc[movie_id, user_rated_movies['movieId']]
    
    user_ratings = user_rated_movies.set_index('movieId')['rating']
    ratings = pd.DataFrame({'similarity': similarity, 'rating': user_ratings})
    
    # drop movies without a similarity or rating
    # sort by similarity - keep just the top k movies
    ratings = ratings.dropna().sort_values(by='similarity', ascending=False).head(k)
    
    # divide by zero check
    if ratings['similarity'].sum() == 0:
        return np.nan
    # return weighted average of ratings
    return np.average(ratings['rating'], weights=ratings['similarity'])

In[111]:
user_similarity_matrix = pd.DataFrame(cosine_similarity(filled_matrix), index=user_movie_matrix.index, columns=user_movie_matrix.index)

def predict_rating_collaborative(user_id, movie_id, k=20):
    if user_id not in user_similarity_matrix.index:
        print("user not found")
        return np.nan
    if movie_id not in user_movie_matrix.columns:
        print("movie not found")
        return np.nan
    
    similar_users = user_similarity_matrix[user_id].drop(index=user_id)
    # find who has rated the movie
    have_rated = user_movie_matrix[user_movie_matrix[movie_id].notna()].index
    similar_users = similar_users.loc[similar_users.index.intersection(have_rated)]
    
    if have_rated.empty:
        print(f"movie {movie_id} was never rated in training")
    else:
        print(f"movie {movie_id} was rated by {len(have_rated)} users")
    if similar_users.empty:
        print(f"no similar users have rated movie {movie_id}")
        return np.nan
    # top 5 most similar
    top_users = similar_users.sort_values(ascending=False).head(k)
    ratings = user_movie_matrix.loc[top_users.index, movie_id]
    # div by 0
    if top_users.sum() == 0:
        return np.nan
    # average the ratings of the top movies (using dot product)
    return np.dot(top_users, ratings) / top_users.sum()
In[112]:
# combine predictions from collaborative filtering and content based filtering
# weighting initially: 0.5 each (cb_weight, cf_weight)
def hybrid_prediction(user_id, movie_id, k=20, cb_weight=0.5, cf_weight=0.5, cb_pred=None, cf_pred=None):
    # was running into an issue after adding tag logic where
    # i think the predictions were being ran twice because of how i had the loop setup
    # modified method to take in pred as parameter instead
    if cb_pred is None:
        cb_pred = predict_rating_content_based(user_id, movie_id, k)
    if cf_pred is None:
        cf_pred = predict_rating_collaborative(user_id, movie_id, k)
    
    # if one or the other prediction is null, return the other one (attempt at fixing the not found issue)
    if np.isnan(cb_pred) and np.isnan(cf_pred):
        return np.nan
    elif np.isnan(cb_pred):
        return cf_pred
    elif np.isnan(cf_pred):
        return cb_pred
    else:
        return cb_weight * cb_pred + cf_weight * cf_pred

# init empty prediction list
predictions = []

missing_movies = set(test_df['movieId']) - set(user_movie_matrix.columns)
print(f"{len(missing_movies)} of {test_df['movieId'].nunique()} test movies are missing from training.")

# use the hybrid modelrating on test pairs
for i, row in test_df.iterrows():
    user_id, movie_id = row['userId'], row['movieId']
    cb_pred = predict_rating_content_based(user_id, movie_id, k=20)
    cf_pred = predict_rating_collaborative(user_id, movie_id, k=20)
    pred = hybrid_prediction(user_id, movie_id, k=20, cb_pred=cb_pred, cf_pred=cf_pred)
    #if i < 10:  # DEBUGGING print sample diagnostics only for first 10 rows
    #    print(f"User {user_id}, Movie {movie_id}  CB: {cb_pred}, CF: {cf_pred}, Hybrid: {pred}")
    predictions.append(pred)

# for the longest time i couldnt figure out why only 10 movies were being caught by the collaborative filtering
# (hence all the debugging nonsense and theres probably a few other things coded in that arent needed anymore from testing around a bunch)
# turns out answer was the most obvious one all along and its just a sparsity issue
# ie not enough users have rated enough overlapping movies
# increasing k neighbors does not seem to do anything
# might mean that switching to USER BASED collab filtering would work better
# idea: users rate few movies -> but users might rate the SAME few movies
